✦ The login page UI features a split design with a vibrant, illustrative background on the left and a functional
  login form on the right.

  Background:
  The left side of the screen is dominated by a stylized illustration of a person in a yellow kayak, actively
  paddling through blue water. The water is depicted with various shades of blue, creating a sense of movement
  and depth, with white wavy lines representing splashes or currents. The kayaker is wearing a white
  long-sleeved top, blue gloves, and an orange helmet, matching the yellow of the kayak. The overall style of
  the illustration is flat and vector-based, with clean lines and a modern, slightly abstract feel. The
  background color behind the illustration appears to be a very light blue or off-white, providing a soft
  contrast.

  Login Form:
  The login form is contained within a large, rounded rectangular card positioned on the right side of the
  screen.
   * Container: The card itself is a prominent, solid yellow color, with significantly rounded corners, giving
     it a friendly and approachable look.
   * Title: At the top of the card, centered, is the text "Login to continue" in a dark, possibly black or very
     dark blue, sans-serif font.
   * Input Fields: Below the title are two input fields for "Username/Email" and "Password".
       * Each input field is a white, rounded rectangle, slightly inset from the yellow background of the card.
       * They feature subtle grey placeholder text.
       * The "Username/Email" field has a small, dark user icon (person silhouette) to its left.
       * The "Password" field has a small, dark eye icon (indicating show/hide password functionality) to its
         left.
   * Options: Below the input fields, there are two options arranged horizontally:
       * "Remember me": This is accompanied by a circular radio button outline.
       * "Forget password?": This is plain text, likely a clickable link, aligned to the right. Both texts are
         in a dark, sans-serif font.
   * Login Button: A large, dark blue (almost navy) rectangular button with rounded corners is centrally placed
     below the options. It contains the word "Login" in white, bold, sans-serif text.
   * Social Login: Below the main login button, there's a smaller text "or sign up using" followed by two
     circular icons for social media logins: a Facebook 'f' logo and a Twitter bird logo. These icons are dark
     blue on a white background, or possibly white on a dark blue background, consistent with the button color.

  Overall Aesthetic:
  The UI uses a bright and inviting color palette, primarily yellow and various shades of blue, with white
  accents. The rounded corners throughout the design contribute to a soft and modern aesthetic. The combination
  of a playful illustration and a clean, functional form creates a balanced and user-friendly interface.

  on the right.

  Background:
  The left side of the screen is dominated by a stylized illustration of a person in a yellow kayak, actively paddling
  through blue water. The water is depicted with various shades of blue, creating a sense of movement and depth, with white
   wavy lines representing splashes or currents. The kayaker is wearing a white long-sleeved top, blue gloves, and an
  orange helmet, matching the yellow of the kayak. The overall style of the illustration is flat and vector-based, with
  clean lines and a modern, slightly abstract feel. The background color behind the illustration appears to be a very light
   blue or off-white, providing a soft contrast.

  Login Form:
  The login form is contained within a large, rounded rectangular card positioned on the right side of the screen.
   * Container: The card itself is a prominent, solid yellow color, with significantly rounded corners, giving it a
     friendly and approachable look.
   * Title: At the top of the card, centered, is the text "Login to continue" in a dark, possibly black or very dark blue,
     sans-serif font.
   * Input Fields: Below the title are two input fields for "Username/Email" and "Password".
       * Each input field is a white, rounded rectangle, slightly inset from the yellow background of the card.
       * They feature subtle grey placeholder text.
       * The "Username/Email" field has a small, dark user icon (person silhouette) to its left.
       * The "Password" field has a small, dark eye icon (indicating show/hide password functionality) to its left.
   * Options: Below the input fields, there are two options arranged horizontally:
       * "Remember me": This is accompanied by a circular radio button outline.
       * "Forget password?": This is plain text, likely a clickable link, aligned to the right. Both texts are in a dark,
         sans-serif font.
   * Login Button: A large, dark blue (almost navy) rectangular button with rounded corners is centrally placed below the
     options. It contains the word "Login" in white, bold, sans-serif text.
   * Social Login: Below the main login button, there's a smaller text "or sign up using" followed by two circular icons for
      social media logins: a Facebook 'f' logo and a Twitter bird logo. These icons are dark blue on a white background, or
     possibly white on a dark blue background, consistent with the button color.

  Overall Aesthetic:
  The UI uses a bright and inviting color palette, primarily yellow and various shades of blue, with white accents. The
  rounded corners throughout the design contribute to a soft and modern aesthetic. The combination of a playful
  illustration and a clean, functional form creates a balanced and user-friendly interface.

╭─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮
│  > which line would help me move the login component towards the right  │
╰─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

✦ To move the login component towards the right, you need to modify the justifyContent property of the Box component that
  directly wraps your Paper (login form).

  Currently, this Box has justifyContent: 'center':

   1       <Box
   2         sx={{
   3           display: 'flex',
   4           justifyContent: 'center', // This line centers the login form horizontally
   5           alignItems: 'center',
   6           p: 2,
   7         }}
   8       >

  To move the login component to the right, you should change this line to:

   1           justifyContent: 'flex-end', // This will align the login form to the right

  If you want to add some space from the right edge, you can also add pr (padding-right) to this Box or mr
  (margin-right) to the Paper component itself.

│  > now tell me how to name them properly  │
╰───────────────────────────────────────────╯

✦ To name files and folders properly, follow these general best practices:

   1. Be Descriptive and Clear: Names should clearly indicate the content or purpose.
       * Good: UserProfileService.ts, LoginButton.tsx, calculate_total.py
       * Bad: stuff.js, btn.jsx, calc.py

   2. Be Consistent: Choose a naming convention and stick to it throughout your project. Common conventions include:
       * kebab-case (all lowercase, words separated by hyphens): Often used for CSS classes, file names in web projects
         (e.g., my-component.css, user-profile.html).
       * snake_case (all lowercase, words separated by underscores): Common in Python, Ruby, and for database column
         names (e.g., user_data.py, process_image.rb).
       * camelCase (first word lowercase, subsequent words capitalized): Common for variables and functions in JavaScript
         (e.g., myVariable, getUserData).
       * PascalCase (first letter of each word capitalized): Common for classes, components, and types in many languages
         (e.g., MyComponent.tsx, UserService.java).

   3. Be Concise: While descriptive, avoid excessively long names.
       * Good: AuthService.ts, Dashboard.tsx
       * Bad: AuthenticationAndAuthorizationService.ts, MainApplicationDashboardPage.tsx

   4. Use Standard Folder Names: For common project structures, use widely recognized names.
       * src: Source code
       * dist or build: Compiled/built output
       * components: Reusable UI components
       * utils or helpers: Utility functions
       * config: Configuration files
       * public: Static assets served directly
       * tests or __tests__: Test files

   5. Avoid Special Characters and Spaces: Stick to alphanumeric characters, hyphens, and underscores. Spaces can cause
      issues in command lines and URLs.
       * Good: my-document.pdf, image_01.jpg
       * Bad: my document.pdf, image#1.jpg

   6. Use `index` for Entry Points: In directories, index.js, index.ts, index.html often denote the main entry point or
      default file.

   7. Consider Case Sensitivity: While Windows is generally case-insensitive, Linux and macOS are case-sensitive. To avoid
      issues when collaborating or deploying, treat file names as case-sensitive (e.g., MyFile.js is different from
      myfile.js).

   8. Version Control Friendly: Keep names stable. Renaming files frequently can complicate version control history.

  By following these guidelines, you'll create a more organized, readable, and maintainable project.
